<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I would definitely skip S.E.'s "Taming the Star Runner". When i first read it, I couldn't take how boring I found it. Don't let that comment sway you<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I would definitely skip S.E.'s "Taming the Star Runner". When i first read it, I couldn't take how boring I found it. Don't let that comment sway you though if you like "city bad boy turned farm boy" kind of stories. <br />I would suggest Tex, or that was then, this is now. They're both pretty great (and an older Ponyboy's even in That was then...).<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/435664551?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 16, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3147703-rainbow" class="user" title="Rainbow">Rainbow</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13418958-the-outsiders" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer435664551">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7601036798065291765">This book is part of a very romantic scene in my third book (Fangirl) -- so I decided to reread it.<br /><br />So good.<br /><br />SO GOOD!<br /><br />I was struck by what an EXHALE it is. It comes out in one long breath. Sometimes it doesn't feel like a novel; it feels more like a story that someone is telling you. And they're talking a little too fast. But still -- SO GOOD. <br /><br />The voice is just seamless ...<br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_119831133">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119831133" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/45618-karen" class="left imgcol" title="karen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451916298p2/45618.jpg" alt="karen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/119831133?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 28, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/45618-karen" class="user" title="karen">karen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/176108.The_Outsiders" title="Paperback 9780142407332" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=and-so-this-is-grad-school" class="actionLinkLite">and-so-this-is-grad-school</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya" class="actionLinkLite">why-yes-i-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer119831133">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12929211601808984909"><em>the outsiders</em> is a book about a group of youthful greasers living in oklahoma, and about their struggles to exist in a society that seems designed to dismiss them. <br /><br /><em>oklahoma</em> is also the name of a popular musical.<br /><br />draw your own conclusions, or continue reading.<br /><br />see, i don't know from oklahoma in the sixties. maybe that is a place where street toughs call their little brothers "honey" and "baby" and enjoy sunsets and stars and reading margaret mitchell aloud to one another and who recite robert frost</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12929211601808984909"><em>the outsiders</em> is a book about a group of youthful greasers living in oklahoma, and about their struggles to exist in a society that seems designed to dismiss them. <br /><br /><em>oklahoma</em> is also the name of a popular musical.<br /><br />draw your own conclusions, or continue reading.<br /><br />see, i don't know from oklahoma in the sixties. maybe that is a place where street toughs call their little brothers "honey" and "baby" and enjoy sunsets and stars and reading margaret mitchell aloud to one another and who recite robert frost in quiet moments. maybe they do gymnastics before what they call "skin fighting" with the local rival boys. maybe they cry and snuggle together in bed at night and hold each other through hard times.<br /><br />not that there is anything wrong with that.<br /><br />it just seems to be queer behavior for a gang of juvenile delinquents.<br /><br />what?? no, i didn't mean <em>queer</em> like that. no, really, i just meant <em>odd</em>. but, now that you mention it. huh. yeah, it does seem a little queer. who knew that boys in leather could have a queer connotation?? <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398682455i/9449695.jpg" /><br /><br />and putting on tight t-shirts that show off every muscle before they go to meet the other boys? and making sure to fix their hair?? no, that's just what it says. in the book.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.sling.com/video/show/26463/90/Hot-Cops">these are their modern-day equivalents</a><br /><br />maybe this is just what happens when a teen girl writes this kind of material, tomboy or not. i had seen the movie before, so i knew it was about pretty boys fighting, but there is a lot more at work here, subtextually. i have also seen <em>rumble fish</em>, which is an awful movie based on another hinton book that is even more... musical, but is an excuse to look at this:<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339078i/695973.jpg" /><br /><br />and how is tom waits in <em>both</em> movies?<br /><br />but all of that is just me giggling.<br /><br />what is more interesting, from a serious <em>literary</em> perspective is just an observation from reading this, <em>the pigman</em>, and revisiting <em>the chocolate war</em> and <em>catcher in the rye</em> for this portion of my young adult readers' advisory class which will meet this tuesday where we will discuss the "classics" of teen fiction. (and i know <em>catcher</em> wasn't specifically produced for a teen audience, but it is on the damn syllabus and if it makes you happier, i will call this "the teen in literature" instead) <br /><br />in the fifties and sixties, there was seemingly more free-floating apprehension and fear: the a-bomb, the draft, various factors contributed to this fear of an imminent death beyond anyone's control. all this anxiety and fear of the establishment created a more pronounced sense of "us" and "them" that i think i blabbed on a little in the pigman review, but children were just treated like smaller adults, really. and the literature reflects this. all of these books seem to emphasize a value placed on the preservation of childhood innocence - staying gold, protecting a younger sister from the taint of phoniness, encouraging kids to act like kids and roller skate through the house and disregard the parental restrictions in this one safe place... <br /><br />now, the boundaries are blurrier - girls are getting their periods at 8, and grown men in suits are playing video games on the subway. the distinctions are less clear. and a lot of teen fiction today is more escapist in nature, less didactic. teens don't need to be told to value their childhood anymore because, don't worry, it will never end. <br /><br />peter pan FTW!!<br /><br />this all means nothing, except it is something i noticed. sorry for blabbing on...<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12929211601808984909">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_109574241">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109574241" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2863914-j" class="left imgcol" title="j"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1407175214p2/2863914.jpg" alt="j" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/109574241?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 12, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2863914-j" class="user" title="j">j</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14870.The_Outsiders" title="Paperback 9780143039853" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to j by: </span>
      Donna
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2863914-j?shelf=2010" class="actionLinkLite">2010</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2863914-j?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2863914-j?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2863914-j?shelf=52-in-2010" class="actionLinkLite">52-in-2010</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2863914-j?shelf=disaffected-youth" class="actionLinkLite">disaffected-youth</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2863914-j?shelf=stay-gold-ponyboy-stay-gold" class="actionLinkLite">stay-gold-ponyboy-stay-gold</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2863914-j?shelf=30-day-book-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">30-day-book-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer109574241">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5511255598243812633">Stay gold, Ponyboy. Stay gold.<br /><br />***********<br /><br />The Outsiders is a book about sensitive teenage boys who alternately get into gang fights, hug one another, and burst into tears. They also spend more time than you might expect ruminating on how the tightness of a t-shirt might enhance the rippling musculature of a steely-eyed fellow gang member (this is where Stephanie Meyer got the idea for how to characterize Edward). Even though they're always complimenting each other's hair and doing gymnastics, it'</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5511255598243812633">Stay gold, Ponyboy. Stay gold.<br /><br />***********<br /><br />The Outsiders is a book about sensitive teenage boys who alternately get into gang fights, hug one another, and burst into tears. They also spend more time than you might expect ruminating on how the tightness of a t-shirt might enhance the rippling musculature of a steely-eyed fellow gang member (this is where Stephanie Meyer got the idea for how to characterize Edward). Even though they're always complimenting each other's hair and doing gymnastics, it's not gay at all because it takes place in 1965, shortly after James Dean had made crying and homoerotic tension cool.<br /><br />This is the kind of book that teachers like to assign to 7th graders (or dumb high schoolers) because it offers up a lot of THEMES about how EVERYONE IS DIFFERENT BUT STILL THE SAME, and teachers feel pretty safe giving a quiz on that because even the stupidest kid can figure it out, as every few paragraphs the narrator will just go ahead and state it outright, like this: "Even though we're Greasers and they're Socs, I guess in the end, we all look at the same sunset." (Sample essay question: What did Ponyboy mean when he said that everyone looked at the same sunset? And all you have to do to get it right is repeat the first half of the sentence.)<br /><br />As a narrator, Ponyboy kept reminding me of Holden Caulfied, if Holden was poor and actually managed to do anything interesting with his evenings. But maybe that just has to do with the time period and the fact that they both say stuff like "I was just about bawling my eyes out, to tell you the truth" every few pages, except Ponyboy is doing it because his best friend knifed someone and then died of a broken back and being on fire, and Holden is just sad because his roommate smells bad (oh and I guess his brother got cancer and died pffffft). I do think they would get along if they ever met, and maybe make out a little bit.<br /><br />I love the last few sentences of every chapter, where SE Hinton trots out her corniest stuff. Chapter 7: "Socs were just guys after all. Things were rough all over, but it was better that way. That way you could tell the other guy was human too." Chapter 8: "'Thanks, Ponyboy.' She smiled through her tears. 'You dig okay.' She had green eyes. I went on, walking home slowly." Oh and it doesn't come at the end of a chapter but: "Not even the rattling of the train could keep me awake, and I went to sleep in a hoodlum's jacket, with a gun lying next to my hand." There's also the best deathbed speech in all of teen literature (probably), which goes like this: "INTERPRETS THEMATICALLY RELEVANT POEM" (DIES).<br /><br />So somehow I never read this in middle school, and when I read it now, I just end up giggling at half of the overwrought emotion (which happened with Catcher in the Rye too, but there I'm going to assume Salinger was writing on multiple levels, because he was a competent adult, whereas The Outsiders was written by someone Holden's age). But it's still a pretty awesome book.<br /><br />EDITED to add that this Penguin edition makes the book seem really classy, which is nice, but Jodi Picoult's introduction is kind of a joke. She basically asked her 14-year-old son to write a book report and quoted excerpts.<br /><br /><em>Facebook 30 Day Book Challenge Day 6: Favorite young adult book.</em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5511255598243812633">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_7203635">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7203635" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/94054-briynne" class="left imgcol" title="Briynne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1225157665p2/94054.jpg" alt="Briynne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/7203635?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 03, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/94054-briynne" class="user" title="Briynne">Briynne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/231804.The_Outsiders" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780140385724" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7203635">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4564207360320055282">I'm a little horrified at myself for not having this book up before now. We had a discussion about it in class today, and I had to write this as soon it was over. I wish there were more stars to give The Outsiders, but five will have to do. I love this book, and have loved it faithfully since I read it in sixth grade - I must have read it a dozen times, and possibly more. I can quote long sections of the book. I was obsessed, and to some degree still am. <br /><br />It's not a good book by any literary stan</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4564207360320055282">I'm a little horrified at myself for not having this book up before now. We had a discussion about it in class today, and I had to write this as soon it was over. I wish there were more stars to give The Outsiders, but five will have to do. I love this book, and have loved it faithfully since I read it in sixth grade - I must have read it a dozen times, and possibly more. I can quote long sections of the book. I was obsessed, and to some degree still am. <br /><br />It's not a good book by any literary standard, really. Hinton uses one of those usually awful formulaic introductions that devotes a paragraph to each main character, explicitly describing their characteristics, history, and appearance. When I think of it objectively, it's almost as bad as that awful, awful introductory second chapter of the Babysitters Club books that repeats in every installment. <br /><br />I think the point is, though, that I just don't care. In fact, I adore the writing even though it is obvious. Maybe because I first read it when I was eleven and that sort of writing just seemed clear and to-the-point. At any rate, I don't think it suffers too badly from the style, and if anything it benefits from the authenticity of a teenage author. <br /><br />I can't even begin to say what it was about this book that caught my interest and imagination so completely. I liked the otherness of it - I had never experienced anything like these boys dealt with. Not the pervasive fear and violence, not the absentee, non-existent, or abusive parents, and definitely not the fascinating siege-mentality camaraderie that existed in their group. <br /><br />The best part of the book, without any doubt, is the characters she has created. I love them all, with the exception of Steve. They are wonderful and so sympathetic, with their odd names and ill-fated lives. I hope for the ending to change every time I read it. Ponyboy's voice, which narrates the story, has a beautiful vulnerability and honesty that makes the story believable. He's often confused, hurt, scared, sorry, and just feels like things are wrong; but, he's also brave and kind and takes chances on people. I think that Hinton's allowing her main character to be a real person, who is more often than not unsure of everything he does, gives the book its credibility with teenagers. <br /><br />Fantastic, must-read, childhood-defining book. Reading Hinton's "That Was Then, This is Now" is worth it just for the few brief cameos a slightly older Ponyboy makes throughout the story. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4564207360320055282">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer12494911">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14945245202281183834">I loved The Outsiders when I read it as a teen and again when I read it just a few months ago. S. E. Hinton created a believable and engaging cast of characters who struggle with conflict in and out of their gang and learn the meaning of friendship and family. A very moving and enjoyable story!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_392416296">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/392416296" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar" class="left imgcol" title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452178371p2/11183856.jpg" alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/392416296?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 08, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar" class="user" title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7840334-the-outsiders" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2014" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer392416296">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14653784535104752051">Find all of my reviews at: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/" target="_blank">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://imgur.com/kSRbvx9"> <img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412779351ra/11421870.gif" /></a><br /><br /><strong> <em> “Nature’s first green is gold, <br />Her hardest hue to hold. <br />Her early leaf’s a flower; <br />But only so an hour. <br />Then leaf subsides to leaf. <br />So Eden sank to grief, <br />So dawn goes down to day.<br />Nothing gold can stay.” </em> </strong><br /><br />Last week my son came home from school and informed me he had a homework assignment about the book his class is reading as a group. Said child was forlorn that he would be unable to complete the assignment as the editions of the bo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14653784535104752051">Find all of my reviews at: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/" target="_blank">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://imgur.com/kSRbvx9">
  <img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412779351ra/11421870.gif" /></a><br /><br /><strong>
  <em> “Nature’s first green is gold, <br />Her hardest hue to hold. <br />Her early leaf’s a flower; <br />But only so an hour. <br />Then leaf subsides to leaf. <br />So Eden sank to grief, <br />So dawn goes down to day.<br />Nothing gold can stay.” </em>
</strong><br /><br />Last week my son came home from school and informed me he had a homework assignment about the book his class is reading as a group. Said child was forlorn that he would be unable to complete the assignment as the editions of the book were for “class use only” and were not permitted to be taken home. “Never you fear,” I said to the young boy, “for I have a LIBRARY CARD!!!!!!” (while actually freaking out that I might have to: (i) change out of my “comfy” clothes, (ii) move my slothlike self off of the sofa after a hard day at work, or (iii) embarrass the child by refusing to change out of P.J. pants whilst chauffeuring him to pick up a hard copy of the book). I asked the small boy (with much trepidation) “what book do you need?” and he answered <em>“The Outsiders.”</em> I was filled with glee and assured my son I could <strong>easily</strong> help him with any questions about that book as I read it a bunch of times myself 800 years ago when I was a young girl. The boy was dubious, so in order to ease his mind I searched the interwebs and was thrilled to find out <em>The Outsiders</em> was available in Kindle format from the library. Whilst waiting for the book to load on to the Kindle, I turned to my son and said the following words:<br /><br /><strong>
  <em> “When I stepped out into the bright sunlight, from the darkness of the movie house, I had only two things on my mind: Paul Newman and a ride home . . .”</em>
</strong><br /><br />Followed by:<br /><br /><strong> “BLAM! TAKE THAT SUCKA! STILL WANT TO TANGLE WITH THE MEMORY OF THIS OLD LADY? YEAH, I DIDN’T THINK SO, NOW WHAT’S YOUR QUESTION?”</strong><br /><br />The boy was able to pick my geriatric brain for assistance with his homework and it turned out the book wasn’t really a requirement in order to get the assignment done in the first place. (Note to all of you youngsters who do not yet have children of you own – THEY ARE WILEY MOFOS AND EVEN THE MOST HONOR-ROLL-A-RIFIC KID WILL AT SOME POINT GO TO ANY AND ALL LENGTHS TO AVOID HOMEWORK.) Thus, I found myself left with <em>The Outsiders</em> on the Kindle and it was seriously <em>begging</em> me to put down the crappy book I was currently reading and take a trip down memory lane. So that’s just what I did . . . <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://imgur.com/n6DVDf5">
  <img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412779351ra/11421871.gif" /></a><br /><br />It was just as good as I remembered it. <em>The Outsiders</em> is the quintessential teenage story about love and loss and family and right and wrong and good and bad. I read it in an evening, sitting outside during a sunset, as one should do if given the opportunity. It proved to be timeless, it still made me teary-eyed after all these years, and I still thought it had one of the best ensemble cast of characters ever put to paper. <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://imgur.com/ayKY6O5">
  <img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412779351i/11421872._SY540_.png" /></a><br /><br />And then I remembered it was written by a <strong>teenager</strong> - one of those awful things that lives in my house and makes my hair turn gray. So let me wrap up this non-review kind of review with a personal note: To my son, I ask you to recognize everything I do for you is with love, just like Darry Curtis and Ponyboy, and I promise I will do everything in my power to make you “stay gold” as long as possible. <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://imgur.com/Z4cgGOI">
  <img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412779351ra/11421873.gif" /></a><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14653784535104752051">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15348100">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18171761241650569390">I LOVE this book. I don't know why I find it so good. The whole thing just seems so real. It's really exciting, and the characters are all really believable. I like how the story was written by a young author who really knew what she was writing about--she based it partly on the experiences of her friends. It's like people say--"Write what you know." And S.E. Hinton did just that, and did an excellent job. The book does have some corny parts, and is one of very few books that actually made me cr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18171761241650569390">I LOVE this book. I don't know why I find it so good. The whole thing just seems so real. It's really exciting, and the characters are all really believable. I like how the story was written by a young author who really knew what she was writing about--she based it partly on the experiences of her friends. It's like people say--"Write what you know." And S.E. Hinton did just that, and did an excellent job. The book does have some corny parts, and is one of very few books that actually made me cry. But it's really fantastic, and I think everyone in the whole world should read it! (But don't watch the movie. It's awful.) </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/2182608?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 20, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/142816-heavyreader" class="user" title="HeavyReader">HeavyReader</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/231804.The_Outsiders" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780140385724" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/142816-heavyreader?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer2182608">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8408461096963780278">I read this book when I was 13. It moved me so that as soon as I got to the end, I turned back to the beginning and read it straight through again. Of course, all this reading was accompanied by much heartfelt crying.<br /><br />I told my mom that it was my favorite book. She told me it was <strong>not</strong> my favorite book. She really meant it wasn't the most well-written book I had ever read, and she was probably right about that. But no one call tell another person what is or isn't his/her/hir favorite book, because</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8408461096963780278">I read this book when I was 13. It moved me so that as soon as I got to the end, I turned back to the beginning and read it straight through again. Of course, all this reading was accompanied by much heartfelt crying.<br /><br />I told my mom that it was my favorite book. She told me it was <strong>not</strong> my favorite book. She really meant it wasn't the most well-written book I had ever read, and she was probably right about that. But no one call tell another person what is or isn't his/her/hir favorite book, because that's an opinion, objective. I knew that even at age 13. So I argued back and told her that it <strong>was</strong> my favorite book. Of course, this wasn't the first time I had argued with my mother, but it was probably the first time I had argued back with such conviction. I think she knew things were only going to get worse for our mother/daughter relationship.<br /><br />I can't forget that she was a good sport and took me (and my sister, who probably didn't want to be there any more than my mother did) to see the movie adaptation of this book. It was dreadful. I even knew how bad it was at the time, even though I didn't want to admit it.<br /><br />One more note...My cousin LIsa was somewhat obsessed with this book at the same time I was. I don't think she was quite as obsessed with it as I was, but she read it and we talked about it. Now her son is in junior high, and he just read this book as a class assignment. I think that makes me officially old.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8408461096963780278">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer755284228">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8545489652849217834">Expectations scare me... I had heard so many wonderful things about this book. And it’s never a good idea to expect too much, because that’s such a big opportunity for disappointment. So I always prefer to know the least amount possible about any book I’m interested in. However, the insurmountable praise for <em>The Outsiders</em> has always been tough to evade. It’s everywhere.<br /><br />I found that the quality of this book was perfectly evidenced by the fact that the immense expectation and build-up accumulated</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8545489652849217834">Expectations scare me... I had heard so many wonderful things about this book. And it’s never a good idea to expect too much, because that’s such a big opportunity for disappointment. So I always prefer to know the least amount possible about any book I’m interested in. However, the insurmountable praise for <em>The Outsiders</em> has always been tough to evade. It’s everywhere.<br /><br />I found that the quality of this book was perfectly evidenced by the fact that the immense expectation and build-up accumulated throughout the years were so well met by the actual classic worthiness of the story and the way it was told.<br /><br />Loved the simple, original narrative. Great, real, well-developed, relatable characters.<br /><br />This book is heartwarming and heartbreaking... so prepare your heart for the exercise.<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_200259542">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200259542" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn" class="left imgcol" title="Aoibhínn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451237485p2/5799885.jpg" alt="Aoibhínn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/200259542?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 03, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn" class="user" title="Aoibhínn">Aoibhínn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32946.The_Outsiders" title="Paperback 9780141314570" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=2012" class="actionLinkLite">2012</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=physical-books" class="actionLinkLite">physical-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer200259542">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2859498984465432083">Set in a small town in Oklahoma in the 1960's, this novel is narrated by a vulnerable fourteen year old orphan, Ponyboy Curtis, who is a member of the "Greasers". The "Greasers" are a gang of boys from a poor neighbourhood and they've all have had to grow up much too fast in order to survive. They come from broken homes, either have no parents or they're parents are drunks and just don't care about their children. The "Greasers" constantly have to be on their guard against vicious attacks from t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2859498984465432083">Set in a small town in Oklahoma in the 1960's, this novel is narrated by a vulnerable fourteen year old orphan, Ponyboy Curtis, who is a member of the "Greasers". The "Greasers" are a gang of boys from a poor neighbourhood and they've all have had to grow up much too fast in order to survive. They come from broken homes, either have no parents or they're parents are drunks and just don't care about their children. The "Greasers" constantly have to be on their guard against vicious attacks from their rival gang, the "Socs". The "Socs", are a group of higher middle to upper-class boys, who all have designer clothes, cars and are college bound. They are rich kids that have things the "Greasers" can only dream about. The two groups literally live on opposite sides of the tracks and are locked in a long standing battle with each other until one night things go too far and a member of the "Socs" is murdered. <br /><br />This was my first time reading <em>The Outsiders</em>. I never managed to get around to reading it as a teenager but I've heard so many people say it is one of their favourite books so I thought it was about time that I read it finally. And now that I've finished the book I can't believe I waited so long!<br /><br /><em>The Outsiders</em> is a gripping and compelling read which is full of suspense. It was also extremely heart-breaking and touching at times. The novel is very well-written, considering S.E. Hinton was just seventeen years old when she wrote it. I was amazed with the amount of depth and layers in this book. There are some corny scenes and the novel is slightly dated in parts but you have to bear in mind that it was written in the 1960's and most of the popular books, TV shows and movies from back then are considered quite corny now. But the book's message is still the same regardless of how cynical we've all become in the 45 years since this book was written. It shows that whether they are poor or rich, all teenagers are essentially the same. They all have the same concerns, fears, struggles, worries and hopes for the future. <br /><br />The characters are all vivid, realistic and well-developed. I really felt for the characters of Ponyboy, Johnny and Dallas and wanted them to succeed. I found it easy to sympathise with the all main characters, after all, we've all been in at least one situation at some point in our lives where we've been misunderstood, and put down simply because of who we are or aren't. <br /><br />The book really shows the flaws in society's pre-conceptions and prejudices of the various social classes. It teaches you thinks are not always what they seem and it reminds us all not to judge a book by its cover. <br /><br />Five stars! <br /><br /><br />If you liked <em>The Outsiders</em>, you'll like the <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/series/58290-kevin-and-sadie">
  <em>Kevin and Sadie</em>
</a> series by Joan Lingard. The two are quite similar and deal with the same conflicts.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2859498984465432083">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn" class="left imgcol" title="Edward Lorn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1428712174p2/8850418.jpg" alt="Edward Lorn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1138100073?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 10, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn" class="user" title="Edward Lorn">Edward Lorn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/67879.The_Outsiders" title="Audio CD 9780739339015" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8850418-edward-lorn?shelf=audio-books" class="actionLinkLite">audio-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8850418-edward-lorn?shelf=52-in-52-2015" class="actionLinkLite">52-in-52-2015</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1138100073">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13461012153167271933"><em>The Outsiders</em> is on my list of 100 Best Films Ever Made. And I hate Tom Cruise. I hate everything about the man. His religion, his face, his hair, the way he plays the same character in every movie (<em>Tropic Thunder</em> excluded, but that character was just as annoying as regular Tom Cruise, so fuck that guy too), but I can stand him as Steve in the film because he's just kinda... there. I think Matt Dillon and Ralph Macchio steal the show, but that's just me. Anyfloop, that's how I feel about the mov</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13461012153167271933"><em>The Outsiders</em> is on my list of 100 Best Films Ever Made. And I hate Tom Cruise. I hate everything about the man. His religion, his face, his hair, the way he plays the same character in every movie (<em>Tropic Thunder</em> excluded, but that character was just as annoying as regular Tom Cruise, so fuck that guy too), but I can stand him as Steve in the film because he's just kinda... there. I think Matt Dillon and Ralph Macchio steal the show, but that's just me. Anyfloop, that's how I feel about the movie. <br /><br />(For a minute there, I forgot I was reviewing the book...)<br /><br />I suppose the reason I started a review of this book with a comment on the film is because they are not much different from each other. If you're pressed for time, the film will do just fine. Of course, if you want more inner thought and motivation, read the book. <br /><br />Continuing the comparison of film and book (why the fuck not, right?), I believe that the movie handles <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Dally's death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> better than the book. In the novel, it's glossed over and damn near cast aside. Considering I loved that character, I gotta put the film above the book. Sorry, purists, but my honest opinion is my honest opinion, and you have every right to be wrong. So be wrong <em>over there</em>.<br /><br />The audiobook is serviceable but nothing special. I swapped between the text and the audio because the narrator, at times, drove me crazy. Jim Fyfe is all right, I suppose, but his faux-hick accent was quite over the top in places, and I couldn't stand his performance of Dally. You might not become as annoyed, but I live in Alabama Country and I deal with necks o' red more than any sane human should. So, if'n you unt to, give this 'ere audiobook a try, 'cause we all knows ya can't read words good.<br /><br />In summation: This is a classic. Read it. 156 pages isn't going to kill you, even if you have seen the movie. The audiobook can be annoying if you don't like hillbilly vernacular, so don't say I didn't warn you.<br /><br /><strong>Final Judgment: Johnny's letter makes me cry.</strong><br /><br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_60116386">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60116386" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2431009-jacqueline" class="left imgcol" title="Jacqueline"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1353275466p2/2431009.jpg" alt="Jacqueline" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/60116386?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 26, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2431009-jacqueline" class="user" title="Jacqueline">Jacqueline</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/231804.The_Outsiders" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780140385724" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer60116386">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12542636997388248937">I am currently 15, and my aunt gave me this book when I was about 12. When I got the book, I put on a happy face and said I as excited to read it. But honestly I did not want to read a book about boys in a bad part of town and about street fights. But my aunt kept asking me if I read it, and after a few months I picked up the book, and from there, I couldn't put it down. This book was so inspirational and great. I loved every one of the characters. My favorite characters were definitely Johnny a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12542636997388248937">I am currently 15, and my aunt gave me this book when I was about 12. When I got the book, I put on a happy face and said I as excited to read it. But honestly I did not want to read a book about boys in a bad part of town and about street fights. But my aunt kept asking me if I read it, and after a few months I picked up the book, and from there, I couldn't put it down. This book was so inspirational and great. I loved every one of the characters. My favorite characters were definitely Johnny and Dallas though. If you are ever hesitant about reading this book, don't second guess it like I did. <br /><br />The story is so real. Things happen, people die. When you read this book, you leave your living room, and you end up in a different, scary world. You read a story that people like you are actually living. And that's the scary part. I cried in this book, laughed a few times, were amused by the characters, and hated some too. This book is not my style, but I thank my aunt for introducing me to this book, that I would never dare try on my own. This book is fantastic and I have nothing but great words to say. I can't think of one flaw, it is great. Give it the chance it deserves. I am in love with this book and it is my favorite book. This book was absolutely great and deserves all the attention it gets. Read this book. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12542636997388248937">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3700948056247468896"><br />Title: The Outsiders<br />Type: Standalone<br />Author: S.E. Hinton<br />First Published On : April 24, 1967<br />Rating: 5 stars<br /><br />“<em>Nothing Stay Forever"<br />"Nature’s first green is gold,<br />"Her hardest hue to hold.<br />"Her early leaf’s a flower;<br />"But only so an hour.<br />"Then leaf subsides to leaf.<br />"So Eden sank to grief,<br />"So dawn goes down today.<br />"Nothing gold can stay<em>’’.<br /><br />-- Robert Frost<br /><br />“I've been thinking about it, and that poem, that guy that wrote it, he meant you're gold when you're a kid, like green. When you're a kid everything's ne</em></em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3700948056247468896"><br />Title: The Outsiders<br />Type: Standalone<br />Author: S.E. Hinton<br />First Published On : April 24, 1967<br />Rating: 5 stars<br /><br />“<em>Nothing Stay Forever"<br />"Nature’s first green is gold,<br />"Her hardest hue to hold.<br />"Her early leaf’s a flower;<br />"But only so an hour.<br />"Then leaf subsides to leaf.<br />"So Eden sank to grief,<br />"So dawn goes down today.<br />"Nothing gold can stay<em>’’.<br /><br />-- Robert Frost<br /><br />“I've been thinking about it, and that poem, that guy that wrote it, he meant you're gold when you're a kid, like green. When you're a kid everything's new, dawn. It's just when you get used to everything that it's day. Like the way you dig sunsets, Pony. That's gold. Keep that way, it's a good way to be”<br /><br />---Johnny Cade<br /><br />“Can you see the sunset real good on the West side? You can see it on the East side too.”<br /><br />---Ponyboy Curtis<br /><br /> In the city where Ponyboy has grown up, there are two major groups of people--the greasers and the socs(Pronounced as Soches). Ponyboy Curtis is a greaser. He comes from a lower-class family and he wears his hair long and greased. His parents both died in a car accident when he was young , He lives with his two older brothers, Darry and Sodapop and they take care of ponyboy like anything, and the rest of the greasers in the neighborhood stick together and lives like a family.<br /><br />The socs live on the west side of town, and they seem to have everything going for them. They are rich and have their own cars. They have nice clothes and nice girlfriends, and their parents give them everything they could ever want and never set any limits for them. Socs takes special pleasure in harassing or beating up the greasers when they’re drunk. The two groups are constantly fighting,and the socs usually win no matter what.<br /><br />16 year old Johnny Cade is the best friend of Ponyboy. Johnny has a really rough life. According to Pony, sixteen-year-old Johnny looks like "a little dark puppy that has been kicked too many times and is lost in a crowd of strangers".His parents are always abusing him and they don’t give a damn about him.To make things even worse he was badly beaten up by a group socs one day and lives in a constant state of fear thereafter.<br /><br />One night Ponyboy is out with Johnny, and they are attacked by a group of drunk socs. One of them holds Ponyboy's head in a fountain and would have drowned him, but Johnny stabs him to make him stop. The boy dies, and Johnny and Ponyboy go on hiding.<br /><br />I liked Ponyboy just fine but it is his brothers and rest of the gang I loved more.Like for instance,Ponyboy never understand the reason why Darry always yells at him and belives his big brother hates him when in reality he is giving up everything just so he can send Ponyboy to college.Johnny was an interesting character,even if he didn’t go to school,he was wiser than Ponyboy.I loved how Soda and Darry always cared for Ponyboy and Dallas Winston,he is like the real hero of the story.I loved this book so much i couldn’t put it down. 5 Bold and Beautiful stars for The Outsiders and yeah ''Stay gold, Ponyboy, stay gold.”<br /><br /><br /><img class="hostedImg escapedImg" style=";display:none;" src="http://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435852947r/15382080.gif?v=1452562095443" /><img class="escapedImg loadingImg" src="/assets/loading-trans.gif" /><br /><br /><br /></em></em></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_17747648">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17747648" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/903390-werner" class="left imgcol" title="Werner"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1216337931p2/903390.jpg" alt="Werner" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/17747648?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 05, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/903390-werner" class="user" title="Werner">Werner</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/231804.The_Outsiders" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780140385724" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Both teen and adult fiction readers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Werner by: </span>
      One of my grandnieces, Alicia
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer17747648">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14851772346163695130">While the setting of this brilliant novel is presumably Hinton's native Tulsa or modeled closely on it, and the specific social circumstances of the teen milieu she depicts, with its sharp and often violent class conflict between the spoiled, nihilistic upper crust versus the angry, socially/economically circumscribed white underclass, may (or in some places, may not) have changed since the 60s, the themes she addresses here are absolutely universal and timeless: the universality of human feelin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14851772346163695130">While the setting of this brilliant novel is presumably Hinton's native Tulsa or modeled closely on it, and the specific social circumstances of the teen milieu she depicts, with its sharp and often violent class conflict between the spoiled, nihilistic upper crust versus the angry, socially/economically circumscribed white underclass, may (or in some places, may not) have changed since the 60s, the themes she addresses here are absolutely universal and timeless: the universality of human feelings, needs, and worth regardless of artificial divisions; the need --and ability-- that every human being has to make his/her own moral decisions and character, regardless of external social circumstances; the value of family ties and friendship; and the transcendent reality that some behaviors are innately right and others wrong, depending on how they treat other people. Through the utterly realistic characters she creates, and the perfectly crafted plot she constructs around them, Hinton conveys her message with an artistry not found among many authors in their 50s and 60s, let alone their teens. She writes thoroughly believable dialogue, and conjures the gritty atmosphere of a lower-class urban neighborhood, without resorting to profanity or cheapening her work with gratuitous sex. And while she conveys a keen consciousness of social injustice, she does not reduce her characters to puppets of social circumstances, nor reduce the personal to the political.<br /><br />Though the publishing industry marketed (and still markets) this book to teens, there is nothing "juvenile" or "kiddish" about it that merits patronizing treatment by older readers or critics. On the contrary, while teen readers continue to embrace the book, it's a work of serious fiction as appropriate for adults as well as any of the books marketed to them --and a better read with more constructive content than most of those, to boot. In short, this is descriptive fiction as it should be written. Forty years is a short period from which to judge the enduring significance of a novel; but I predict that this one <em>will</em> stand the test of time, and that one day a sane critical community (if we ever have one :-)) will rank it as a crown jewel of the Realist tradition, and of American fiction.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14851772346163695130">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_173362735">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173362735" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1500718-ryan" class="left imgcol" title="Ryan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1238846167p2/1500718.jpg" alt="Ryan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/173362735?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 13, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1500718-ryan" class="user" title="Ryan">Ryan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/231804.The_Outsiders" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780140385724" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer173362735">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer674196506133063694">I never read <em>The Outsiders</em>, and I always felt left out because of it.<br /><br />There are many texts like this in North America. A brief list of stories often taught in grades 7 - 9 might include <em>To Kill A Mockingbird</em>, <em>The Giver</em>, and <em>Romeo and Juliet</em>. Believe it or not, there's quite a controversy over this notion.<br /><br />Does everyone need to read <em>The Outsiders</em>?<br /><br />Teachers ask this question quite often, but they're not always given the authority to answer it. Instead, they are asked to teach the stories that are sto</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText674196506133063694">I never read <em>The Outsiders</em>, and I always felt left out because of it.<br /><br />There are many texts like this in North America. A brief list of stories often taught in grades 7 - 9 might include <em>To Kill A Mockingbird</em>, <em>The Giver</em>, and <em>Romeo and Juliet</em>. Believe it or not, there's quite a controversy over this notion.<br /><br />Does everyone need to read <em>The Outsiders</em>?<br /><br />Teachers ask this question quite often, but they're not always given the authority to answer it. Instead, they are asked to teach the stories that are stocked (and which have supporting resources) in the school. Nevertheless, they'll sometimes meet a parent that complains about a book simply because they were taught it in school. Other parents complain when teachers introduce new books that parents did not read in school. It's tricky.<br /><br />But this gets "real" (and potentially expensive) when we start to ask whether a class of students should be required to read the same book. If students are learning to read, shouldn't they just choose books that they want to read?<br /><br />Today, there are teachers that will arrange their course so that students can work on a common theme, but can choose one of several books that speak to that theme to read as part of a group. An uncommon example, but one that I think is quite illustrative, would be to teach Shakespearean tragedy, but to allow groups to choose from <em>Othello</em>, <em>Hamlet</em>, or <em>Macbeth</em>.<br /><br />Other teachers are even more "radical" and allow students to read individually, which can be a nightmare in terms of logistics. And still others feel that there is value in a class of students exploring a text together. This is a traditional view, but not necessarily an incorrect one.<br /><br />At this point in my career, I'm more inclined to organize a class that accommodates every option rather than settling on one. This must sound like a cop-out, but it's actually a sensible conclusion. For example, one advantage is teaching an entire class, then allowing them to work more independently in smaller groups, and then asking them to work as individuals.<br /><br />Although I certainly read books in high school and university that I did not love, I don't regret being asked to respond to any one of them. And upon re-reading those texts, such as <em>Lord of the Flies</em>, I came to enjoy them all the more. And there is certainly value in being asked to stretch our horizons. At other times, I think we realize that we'd be lost in our culture if we couldn't speak to, or respond to, certain novels. For Americans, <em>The Great Gatsby</em> might be a good example. Regardless of our background, many feel that Fitzgerald's treatment of the American Dream is required reading for people to practice citizenship.<br /><br />As for <em>The Outsiders</em>, I'm actually quite sorry that I never read it while in middle school. S.E. Hinton tells the story of the Curtis brothers from the point of view of Ponyboy. (That's his real name.) Ponyboy is a member of the Greaser gang and he and his friends spend their nights watching movies, driving around, and getting into "rumbles." Sometimes, they fight with broken bottles too. The story is compelling, and even moving. Although Ponyboy has the potential to succeed, he may end up abandoning it so he can keep hanging out with the "wrong" crowd, who may be violent but are certainly easy to sympathize with.<br /><br />Still, I'll admit that there is a depth to "stay golden" that would have impressed the 12 year old me. The adult me was more inclined to just "note" that an important metaphor had been issued.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="674196506133063694">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_209555978">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/209555978?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 05, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6040603-demo" class="user" title="Demo">Demo</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone who ever lived.</span></div>

      Teacher

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6040603-demo?shelf=best-male-character" class="actionLinkLite">best-male-character</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer209555978">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8749754979482855207">When my English teacher assigned The Outsiders, I was just like "Whatever." I really didn't care that much about the book and drew a conclusion from the awful opinions I have of <a title="Wuthering Heights by Emily Brontë" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6185.Wuthering_Heights">Wuthering Heights</a> and <a title="The Phantom of the Opera by Gaston Leroux" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/480204.The_Phantom_of_the_Opera">The Phantom of the Opera</a> that me and classics just <em>don't</em> mix.<br /><br />Major book pwn, my friends. I was dead <em>wrong</em>.<br /><br />This book left me slack-jawed. Every single character had such a defined personality. Even better, I could actually <em>understand</em> what Ponyboy was saying! When I was reading Wuthering Heights, I ha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8749754979482855207">When my English teacher assigned The Outsiders, I was just like "Whatever." I really didn't care that much about the book and drew a conclusion from the awful opinions I have of <a title="Wuthering Heights by Emily Brontë" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6185.Wuthering_Heights">Wuthering Heights</a> and <a title="The Phantom of the Opera by Gaston Leroux" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/480204.The_Phantom_of_the_Opera">The Phantom of the Opera</a> that me and classics just <em>don't</em> mix.<br /><br />Major book pwn, my friends. I was dead <em>wrong</em>.<br /><br />This book left me slack-jawed. Every single character had such a defined personality. Even better, I could actually <em>understand</em> what Ponyboy was saying! When I was reading Wuthering Heights, I had to reread sentences like three times before I actually understood the meaning and context. They used words like "methinks" and other dialect that's been dead for a little under a century. With Pony, I understood what he said perfectly! Except when he used double negatives, but that's a different story.<br /><br />What was really fun was that there were no stereotypical personality. Cherry Valance (or whatever her last name is; that isn't important right now) was a NICE cheerleader. Johnny and Pony were WISE teenage boys (which, you have to admit, nearly never happens in today's YA Fiction). Randy was a NICE rich popular boy.<br /><br />But really, with the Cherry thing; I doubt <em>all</em> cheerleaders are stupid or slutty! I mean think of all the negatives toward cheerleaders in books: Emily Asher and Savannah Snow from <a title="Beautiful Creatures (Caster Chronicles, #1) by Kami Garcia" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304335.Beautiful_Creatures__Caster_Chronicles___1_">Beautiful Creatures</a>, Marcie from <a title="Hush, Hush (Hush, Hush, #1) by Becca Fitzpatrick" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664.Hush__Hush__Hush__Hush___1_">Hush, Hush</a>, etc. Usually the entire book I'm going,"Girl,<br /><img width="455" height="300" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359106i/710265.gif" /> "<br /><br />But not for The Outsiders. *happy dance*<br /><br />Speaking of characters, I was a little pissed that <em>both</em> of my favorite characters had to die within a few pages of each other. Surprisingly though, unlike other books where I start bawling my eyes out, I didn't really feel bad about their deaths. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ Johnny didn't have anything to fall back on, besides the gang. He'd be much happier wherever he's going than he was at home. I'm sure of that. Dally technically committed suicide, so it was his own choice. He obviously thought it through and had his reasons, so maybe he thought it was better this way, too. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It had a fantastic ending, either way.<br /><br />That's another thing! The book actually <em>told</em> you what happened after the major "rumble." So many books just cut off directly after the climax (Hear that, <a title="13 to Life (13 to Life, #1) by Shannon Delany" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7230309.13_to_Life__13_to_Life___1_">13 to Life</a> and <a title="Forever (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #3) by Maggie Stiefvater" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9409458.Forever__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___3_">Forever</a>?) and don't clue you in on how the characters end up a month or two after the fact. Do they cope? Do they freak out? Do they celebrate? <br /><br />IMPORTANT QUESTIONS, PEOPLE!!!<br /><br />Oh yeah, about the characters. I keep getting off track. I looked up what they all looked like in the movie... Oh jeez. It's not how I saw them at <em>all.</em> I had a very vivid mental image of Johnny---I knew exactly what he looked like. Fancy black hair, suspicious expression, scared black eyes---I just saw it. And then I saw this:<br /><img width="365" height="486" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359106i/710266.jpg" /><br /><br /><em>Please</em> tell me that wasn't the actual actor they used, that it's just some kid who someone decided looked enough like Johnny to post on Google. Seriously, he looks like he's twelve. Thirteen at most.<br />I also saw this:<br /><img width="208" height="280" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359106i/710267.jpg" /><br />which also doesn't look a thing like my mental image. Except the hair. That was sort of the same hair.<br /><br />I also tried looking up Soda. I don't know if I made it up in my head or if it actually says in the book that he has light blond hair. But I saw the picture and I was like "Um... no."<br /><br />I was thinking more along the lines of Jesse McCartney:<br /><img width="640" height="450" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359106i/710268._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Ahahaha, kidding. You can stop giving me the evil eye now.<br /><br />Anyway, this book is friggin a<em>maz</em>ing. I even added it to my favorites list, which is rather hard to accomplish anymore. <br /><br />5 stars all the way, people!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />I choked on my drink laughing when I saw this:<br /><img width="530" height="388" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359106i/710269.jpg" /><br />*dramatic look*<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90227338" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog" class="left imgcol" title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1366465767p2/1059653.jpg" alt="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/90227338?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog" class="user" title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)">Kelly H. (Maybedog)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32946.The_Outsiders" title="Paperback 9780141314570" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-fiction-and-literature" class="actionLinkLite">what-fiction-and-literature</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-classic" class="actionLinkLite">what-classic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=abandoned" class="actionLinkLite">abandoned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">what-young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer90227338">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9588876118708260733">I finally got the book from the library and have just started it. I'm incredibly impressed that this was penned by a kid in high school. It's very well written. There are bits that feel like a teenager wrote it, but that's a good thing because too often lately I've been reading children's books that feel like a 42 year old wrote them. While it's not bad to be 42 and write for kids, I'm 42 and do so, you don't want to sound 42.<br /><br />I'm also bored. It's not Hinton's fault at all. I'm sure when she wrot</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9588876118708260733">I finally got the book from the library and have just started it. I'm incredibly impressed that this was penned by a kid in high school. It's very well written. There are bits that feel like a teenager wrote it, but that's a good thing because too often lately I've been reading children's books that feel like a 42 year old wrote them. While it's not bad to be 42 and write for kids, I'm 42 and do so, you don't want to sound 42.<br /><br />I'm also bored. It's not Hinton's fault at all. I'm sure when she wrote the book it was a fairly fresh idea, even with West Side Story ten years old already. But now, half a century later, this story has been done to death, with stories that take place in that same era as well as the same plot in more modern times. John Hughes made a fortune off of the idea of the rich kids vs. the outsiders.<br /><br />My experiences weren't like that at all. It had nothing to with wealth but with class. That sometimes corresponds to wealth but not always. For example, I was raised with upper middle-class values but my mom was a single parent so we didn't have a lot of money. At my school, the classes stuck to their own and picked on their own. I was ostracized and picked on by those upper middle class folks, the college bound kids. I was an outsider to both groups. No one went anywhere near our version of the greasers--the "druggies" who may not have done any drugs but they tended to smoke and skip class a lot--they weren't even in our world.<br /><br />One exception was that one "druggie" in my neighborhood started picking on me long before we had such distinctions. He was even a couple of years younger. That continued into high school until one day someone spray-painted "Sow" on the inside of my fence. He used to call me that and he cut through my yard sometimes so I was pretty sure it was he. I went to talk to his father about it who claimed his son had been in the library all afternoon with his mother. (Yeah, right.) But I sent a flower to his homeroom to apologize for accusing him. (He wasn't there, he was cutting class that day.) After that he was nice to me. It was weird.<br /><br />Anyway, I'll keep reading.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9588876118708260733">...more</a>

          </span>

      <a href="/user/show/13346584-ana" class="user" title="Ana">Ana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer440064461">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3099640173840444647">Though I usually prefer romance and fantasy, reading The Outsiders was an amazing experience. It took me by surprise how much I ended up enjoying this book. I loved everything about it - even the character's faults. The book also introduced me to one of my favorite poems, "Nothing Gold Can Stay." Just incredible. <br /><br /><br />Stay gold, Pony Boy, stay gold.</span>

          </span>
        </div>
