<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1089392878">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089392878" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/34715306-jonnie" class="left imgcol" title="Jonnie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450739621p2/34715306.jpg" alt="Jonnie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1089392878?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 22, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/34715306-jonnie" class="user" title="Jonnie">Jonnie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/231804.The_Outsiders" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780140385724" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/34715306-jonnie?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1089392878">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7013559390857467459"><strong>Nothing Gold Can Stay</strong><br /><br /><em>Nature's first green is gold,<br />Her hardest hue to hold.<br />Her early leaf's a flower;<br />But only so an hour.<br />Then leaf subsides to leaf,<br />So Eden sank to grief,<br />So dawn goes down to day<br />Nothing gold can stay.</em><br /><br />— Robert Frost<br /><br />One of my favorite poems was incorporated in this book. One of my favorite actors was mentioned in the first sentence. One of my most lusted-after celebrity men was in the film. Gahd damn, that's gotta say it all, right?<br /><br /><em>The Outsiders</em> is an amazing book. I first picked it</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7013559390857467459"><strong>Nothing Gold Can Stay</strong><br /><br /><em>Nature's first green is gold,<br />Her hardest hue to hold.<br />Her early leaf's a flower;<br />But only so an hour.<br />Then leaf subsides to leaf,<br />So Eden sank to grief,<br />So dawn goes down to day<br />Nothing gold can stay.</em><br /><br />— Robert Frost<br /><br />One of my favorite poems was incorporated in this book. One of my favorite actors was mentioned in the first sentence. One of my most lusted-after celebrity men was in the film. Gahd damn, that's gotta say it all, right?<br /><br /><em>The Outsiders</em> is an amazing book. I first picked it up in High School as a to-read-for-academic-purposes, but because I'm a book whore through and through the joke was on the teachers. I devoured this book in one sweet library-filled day, and let me tell you it was a phenomenal experience. The characters are wonderfully written; I came to know each one quite thoroughly, so the fact that this novel covers one week? Amazing. And the fact that S.E Hinton wrote this when she was 16? <em>Brilliant.</em> <br /><br />Pretty sure at 16 I was still eating dirt. Anyway.<br /><br />Oklahoma, 1960's. The "Greasers" are a gang of underprivileged teens who are constantly under attack by those rich mother fuckers also know as the "Socs", but let's just call them those rich mother fuckers for now. Narrated by 14-year-old Ponyboy Curtis, it weaves an incredible story of friendship and hardship that was just unputdownable.<br /><br />Because I read this for school, I had to scrutinize this on an academic level, and write those god awful essays on themes and symbolism. God forbid we can just read a book and write a three-page essay on how cool it was, am I right!? (I secretly enjoyed them but <em>shhhhh</em>). However, this still didn't stop me from enjoying it and re-reading it a second, and a third time (and simultaneously spooning ice-cream into my mouth while perving on Patrick Swayze. <em>The things I would do to that man...</em>). All pervs aside, this book actually has a pretty strong message, which I will leave you to discover should you choose to read it. <br /><br />And I think you should read it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7013559390857467459">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2951112-amber?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer79594155'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer79594155">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13105288740537742924">"Ew" is the one thing I have to say about this book. Stupid, ew, and "why was I required to read this?"<br /><br />This book really got on my nerves. Why?<br />-NO DESCRIPTIONS. This book showed no promise of detail. There was no description. Nothing.<br />Not to mention-Johnny's death scene? LAME.<br />-THE CHARACTERS-they all bothered me. I think my friend summed it up well when she said, "They are all a bunch of idiots who love each other and sleep together." Their personalities were so shallow they could have been kiddie</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13105288740537742924">"Ew" is the one thing I have to say about this book. Stupid, ew, and "why was I required to read this?"<br /><br />This book really got on my nerves. Why?<br />-NO DESCRIPTIONS. This book showed no promise of detail. There was no description. Nothing.<br />Not to mention-Johnny's death scene? LAME.<br />-THE CHARACTERS-they all bothered me. I think my friend summed it up well when she said, "They are all a bunch of idiots who love each other and sleep together." Their personalities were so shallow they could have been kiddie pools, and they were all over the place.<br />-This book just drug on and on and on.<br /><br />By page 3 I was ready to ditch it.<br /><br />NOT TO MENTION-we studied this for 2 WHOLE MONTHS for school.<br /><br /><br /><br />And I get to read the sequal next year?<br /><br /><br />Oh joy.<br /><br />This book is a hugely dissapointing read. It lived up to zero of my expectations, and if you were on the fence about reading it-look at the character's names. Sodapop. Ponyboy.<br />Serious-leh?<br />This book was supposed to be life changing. Amazing. So good! A book you'd fall in love with. A classic that will leave you wanting more.<br /><br />Well, I say, "I don't think so."<br /><br />Skip out on this one-a classic? I don't think so.<br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_440675269">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440675269" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11818290-sarah" class="left imgcol" title="Sarah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1345181768p2/11818290.jpg" alt="Sarah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/440675269?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 24, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11818290-sarah" class="user" title="Sarah">Sarah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1191522.The_Outsiders" title="Hardcover 9780670532575" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11818290-sarah?shelf=fiction-ya" class="actionLinkLite">fiction-ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11818290-sarah?shelf=library-books" class="actionLinkLite">library-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer440675269">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11432295707610688041">24/11 - This reminded me of a darker, more realistic <em>American Graffiti</em> set in Oklahoma. I don't know much about the state of Oklahoma (or possibly anything about it, seeing as I was under the impression it's a state full of cowboys and horses and ranches), I didn't even know the capital city prior to googling it. I would never have imagined that Oklahoma would have gang wars between the Greasers (I've seen <em>Grease</em> about 50 times, enough to recite most of the dialogue, and <em>American Graffiti</em> twice</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11432295707610688041">24/11 - This reminded me of a darker, more realistic <em>American Graffiti</em> set in Oklahoma. I don't know much about the state of Oklahoma (or possibly anything about it, seeing as I was under the impression it's a state full of cowboys and horses and ranches), I didn't even know the capital city prior to googling it. I would never have imagined that Oklahoma would have gang wars between the Greasers (I've seen <em>Grease</em> about 50 times, enough to recite most of the dialogue, and <em>American Graffiti</em> twice and I had always thought the name 'Greaser' came from their penchant for fixing up cars, not the excess hair gel they used, so that was a lesson I learned) and the Socs. I would have thought that in the 60s Oklahoma was just managing to get sealed roads from one side of the state to the other (no offense to Oklahomans, but your state just isn't in the media all that much here).<br /><br />Reading it in 2015, I thought this was quite a good YA book, but I can't even imagine the reaction from parents in 1967. Gangs, 'rumbles', teenagers exhibiting sexual behaviour, 'heaters' (that was something I didn't understand, the slang term 'heater' for a gun, in fact until it was described as being loaded I actually believed they meant a real heater and thought "Wow, that would be rather ungainly to carry around town"), murderers and their associates 'getting away with the crime'. With all those taboo topics, how on earth did this get past the censors of the day?<br /><br />This is one of the most widely read books among my GR friends, but I hadn't even heard of it till the last year or so and even then only because of my presence on the website. Thank you GR, without you I probably never would've read this book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11432295707610688041">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/356305-sara" class="user" title="Sara">Sara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7047677">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13109024055441895318">The Outsiders is very similar to The West Side Story, it talks about 2 gangs however, in th is story, it’s about the relationships and gap between the rich and poor. The two gangs named, The Greasers and The Socs, are common enemies in their society. However, the love part is very similar to Romeo and Juliet, where one person from each of the gangs or the enemies falls in love with each other. Cherry from the Socs falls in love with Ponyboy and Johnny, Greasers. Like in Romeo and Juliet, it caus</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13109024055441895318">The Outsiders is very similar to The West Side Story, it talks about 2 gangs however, in th is story, it’s about the relationships and gap between the rich and poor. The two gangs named, The Greasers and The Socs, are common enemies in their society. However, the love part is very similar to Romeo and Juliet, where one person from each of the gangs or the enemies falls in love with each other. Cherry from the Socs falls in love with Ponyboy and Johnny, Greasers. Like in Romeo and Juliet, it causes more conflict between one another. <br />	The fight all began when Ponyboy was returning home from a movie and the Socs starts to bully them. They got into a big fight and boys from the Greaser comes to help but the problem did not end there. They started to develop bigger problems because the Greasers were hanging out with the girls, the Socs. Eventually, a lot of things starts to happen, fights breaks out, people dies. Johnny, one of Ponyboy’s friend, killed Bob, one of the Socs, because he was going to kill Ponyboy. So, Ponyboy and Johnny runs away to a church with the help of Dally, another Greaser. They are in the hideout for a week and Dally finally takes Johnny and Ponyboy home. However, on their way home, there was a fire in a children’s school; Ponyboy and Johnny decides to help and save kids. They became heros, but Johnny didn’t turn out good. While he was saving the kids, the roof of the school collapsed on him. It broke his back and eventually died at the end. Additionally, at the end, Ponyboy realizes the greater meaning of life, family. He realize how family and friends meant so much to him. <br />	The point where Ponyboy realize how important family means to him is the part where he finally grows up. He finally understands the bigger meaning of life instead of just violence. The Outsider is very much the same as The West Side Story. The characters deals with the same obstacles, the same people dies, the same situation happens to Johnny, but the names of the characters are very different and the name of the gangs are different too, instead of Greasers and Socs, they have the Jet and Sharks. However, pretty much everything else is the same. <br /><br /> This is like my 4th time reading this book, it is so good!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13109024055441895318">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_676979898">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/676979898" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/350218-booklady" class="left imgcol" title="booklady"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1354374319p2/350218.jpg" alt="booklady" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/676979898?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 14, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/350218-booklady" class="user" title="booklady">booklady</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7840334-the-outsiders" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=classic" class="actionLinkLite">classic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=literature" class="actionLinkLite">literature</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=autobiography" class="actionLinkLite">autobiography</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=adventure" class="actionLinkLite">adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=youth" class="actionLinkLite">youth</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=crime" class="actionLinkLite">crime</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=worth-reading-over-and-over" class="actionLinkLite">worth-reading-over-and-over</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=2013" class="actionLinkLite">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer676979898">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15248090772123972461">I remember growing up as a geeky young teenager I could have written a poem similar to the lyrics in Jordan Pruitt’s song, <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ND2-XCcwzt4">Outside Looking In</a>: <em>‘If you could read my mind, you might see more of me than meets the eye. And you've been all wrong—not who you think I am. You've never given me a chance. You don't know how it feels to be outside the crowd. You don't know what it's like to be left out. And you don't know how it feels to be your own best friend on the outside looking in.’</em> Maybe I'm not th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15248090772123972461">I remember growing up as a geeky young teenager I could have written a poem similar to the lyrics in Jordan Pruitt’s song, <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ND2-XCcwzt4">Outside Looking In</a>: <em>‘If you could read my mind, you might see more of me than meets the eye. And you've been all wrong—not who you think I am. You've never given me a chance. You don't know how it feels to be outside the crowd. You don't know what it's like to be left out. And you don't know how it feels to be your own best friend on the outside looking in.’</em> Maybe I'm not the only one who can relate to those words?<br /><br />We’re all outsiders at some point, to some group—it’s only a question of where and when. Ponyboy, the youngest of the three Curtis boys left orphaned by the automobile accident of their parents finds himself labeled a ‘greaser’ for the way he wears his hair. This automatically puts him in opposition to those known as the ‘Socs’—for Socialites, or the rich kids, in his little patch of a 1960’s Oklahoma town.<br /><br />The two groups, Greasers and Socs could be any two hostile groups in history: Israelites and Egyptians; Greeks and Trojans; Romans and Christians; Native Americans and European settlers; blacks and whites in America or South Africa, the haves and the have-nots, First World inhabitants and those confined to Third World nations. <br /><br />Ponyboy like the other ‘outsiders’ – and even some so-called ‘insiders’ in the story, discover group identity isn’t necessarily a requirement and often not even desirable. He learned that people of the same group—which in this case was his gang—are making similar choices for entirely different reasons:<blockquote>
  <em>‘If everybody jumped in the Arkansas River, ol’ Two-Bit would be right on their heels. I had it then. Soda fought for fun, Steve for hatred, Darry for pride, and Two-Bit for conformity. Why do I fight? I thought and couldn’t think of any real good reason. There isn’t any real good reason for fighting except self-defense.’</em>
</blockquote><em>The Outsiders</em> was first published in 1967 when the author was in her freshman year at the University of Tulsa. I never read it growing up but my husband just told me his high school teacher had them read it because they would be meeting kids like the characters in this book. It’s my wish that all young people would read this book. Even if the groups are no longer called “Greasers” and “Socs”, the issues are still the same. Young people are still writing about, fighting about and dying feeling like Outsiders.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15248090772123972461">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16097231875529134258">Yep, I be the husband. I was in Bountiful, Utah at the time, and my English teacher was a full-blown hippy. Although the book was assigned, I read it</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16097231875529134258">Yep, I be the husband. I was in Bountiful, Utah at the time, and my English teacher was a full-blown hippy. Although the book was assigned, I read it in two days... and related to many, because as an AF kid just moved From Wichita Falls, TX, halfway through the 7th grade, I was DEFNITELY the outsider. Girls used to pull the buzz-cut hair on the back of my head because I was the only one who didn't have long hair; It was also the second time I was physically put on the floor by a punch by a guy twice my size. Caught me in the gut, totally unaware. When we moved to Layton, that made the difference, because there were a lot of other military folks there. I relate to being not one of the group; it's more comfortable for me. And this book showed me that I was not the only one who had troubles. It was a long time before I finally overcame a lot of the issues, but the reality is that book and my teacher sowed deep seeds of self confidence when she showed us how we could be. A must for everyone, even if you are over 50!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16097231875529134258">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/7680286?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 13, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/419381-julie" class="user" title="Julie">Julie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/231804.The_Outsiders" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780140385724" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7680286">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8328105877800579197">This book, which was written in the 1960's, may have well been written today. It describes the many conflicts between gangs, social groups, family violence, and friends. Many emotions and thoughts surround the patrogonist, Ponyboy, who describes ganglife in the city. The book goes into many depths to develop the personality and emotions of every single character, and even from the view of the main character, you know the intellects of every little character. Every emotion is very sicere and well</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8328105877800579197">This book, which was written in the 1960's, may have well been written today. It describes the many conflicts between gangs, social groups, family violence, and friends. Many emotions and thoughts surround the patrogonist, Ponyboy, who describes ganglife in the city. The book goes into many depths to develop the personality and emotions of every single character, and even from the view of the main character, you know the intellects of every little character. Every emotion is very sicere and well portrayed and not a detail is left out. You get a good view of human nature, feelings, and life. The story has a very moving plot that deals with family conflicts, murder, robbery, gang fights, friendship, social status, and loss. It does well at alerting the reader of the seriousness of gang warfare. Even though it expresses the many sad parts of life in the city, it gives a message that there can be hope and there is hope for those who have not lost the fight yet. This is an incredible book and definately worth getting. A must read! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8328105877800579197">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BDUuVA5RJ91S8vNg2ZxXsRj3V/NjT4Rv0HnOfR8B1bNh4RGH/IMzJ94qh9un/bEDUQCU6iqSw8W6cMvv05Qj9g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZCmQXs35KXb4CQDf5hZJSqFcHaAiBCBPzvAHdavVC3kB/a+NPys9jHTRdGSYd6/46KveuWvZZ+Wk+QLnZ0D9PA==')})
  }

Five months later and still 100 miles from land, their ship, Endurance, became trapped in ice. The expedition survived another five months camping on ice floes, followed by a perilous journey through stormy seas to remote and unvisited Elephant Island. In a dramatic climax to this amazing survival story, Shackleton and five others navigated 800 miles of treacherous open ocean in a 20-foot boat to fetch a rescue ship.Shipwreck at the Bottom of the World vividly re-creates one of the most extraordinary adventure stories in history.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/762707.S_E_Hinton">About S.E. Hinton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/762707.S_E_Hinton"><img alt="762707" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1206505616p2/762707.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer12940992637295186950">S.E. Hinton, was and still is, one of the most popular and best known writers of young adult fiction. Her books have been taught in some schools, and banned from others. Her novels changed the way people look at young adult literature. <br /><br />Susan Eloise Hinton was born in Tulsa, Oklahoma. She has always enjoyed reading but wasn't satisfied with the literature that was being written for young adults, wh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12940992637295186950">S.E. Hinton, was and still is, one of the most popular and best known writers of young adult fiction. Her books have been taught in some schools, and banned from others. Her novels changed the way people look at young adult literature. <br /><br />Susan Eloise Hinton was born in Tulsa, Oklahoma. She has always enjoyed reading but wasn't satisfied with the literature that was being written for young adults, which influenced her to write novels like <em>The Outsiders</em>. That book, her first novel, was published in 1967 by Viking.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12940992637295186950">...more</a>

    </div>
